201510	2848	2015-10-28	meeting	YELLEN	President Kocherlakota.	23	2
201510	2849	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201510	2850	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Our first job as a central bank is to maintain the nominal anchor.	23	2
201510	2851	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It is a common belief among citizens in this country that inflation will be at 2 percent over the longer run.	23	2
201510	2852	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I see plenty of evidence to suggest that we’re failing in this task.	23	2
201510	2853	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Inflation has been low for years.	23	2
201510	2854	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Core inflation has been below target for most of the past seven years and is expected to remain low for years to come.	23	2
201510	2855	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Wage and compensation growth both remain subdued and, based on information from our labor contacts, are expected to remain so.	23	2
201510	2856	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Global disinflationary trends are strong and expected to remain so.	23	2
201510	2857	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In my view, financial market data actually provide the most compelling evidence on this point.	23	2
201510	2858	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The low inflation breakevens are sending a clear message.	23	2
201510	2859	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Investors believe that there’s a significant risk that the Federal Reserve will be unwilling to do what is necessary to hit either of its mandates over the longer run.	23	2
201510	2860	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	To reiterate a point that I made yesterday and have made earlier in these meetings, the low risk premiums that have been deduced out of the low breakevens are signaling that people think low inflation is going to take place at the same time as low economic activity.	23	2
201510	2861	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So they view nominal Treasury securities as being a better protection with regard to those low-economic-activity states.	23	2
201510	2862	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That’s what that shrinkage in breakevens is signaling.	23	2
201510	2863	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	What does that mean?	23	2
201510	2864	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It means that investors believe that we’re going to have low economic activity for very long periods of time, taking place at the same time as low inflation.	23	2
201510	2865	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	What is that about?	23	2
201510	2866	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We have control over inflation, especially over long periods of time.	23	2
201510	2867	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That’s a signal that investors do not believe we’re going to do what is necessary to deliver on our inflation goals at the time when there is low economic activity, either because we’re going to face constraints in what we’re able to do or because we’re going to choose not to do it.	23	2
201510	2868	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, Madam Chair, is available evidence definitive that our nominal anchor has slipped from its 2 percent resting place?	23	2
201510	2869	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thankfully, I would say, “Not yet.”	23	2
201510	2870	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But the evidence from around the world and from our own history is clear on this point.	23	2
201510	2871	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If we wait for certainty on this point that inflation expectations have left their mooring, either up or down, we will have waited too long.	23	2
201510	2872	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The Committee needs to respond aggressively now to the risk of credibility loss to avoid facing the certainty of credibility loss.	23	2
201510	2873	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Such a loss of credibility would significantly constrain our ability to support the economy in the face of future adverse shocks, especially in the kind of world we contemplated yesterday, in which r* is persistently low.	23	2
201510	2874	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In view of the risk to our credibility, I would recommend that the FOMC initiate a new round of asset purchases and publicly announce its intention to explore the feasibility of negative interest rates.	23	2
201510	2875	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The Vice Chairman asked for suggestions on what kinds of interventions we might contemplate if needed.	23	2
201510	2876	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think such interventions are needed at this time, so I’m suggesting some.	23	2
201510	2877	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’m obviously not wedded to these particular ones.	23	2
201510	2878	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	There are a number of ways one could proceed.	23	2
201510	2879	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Simply announcing the intention to never halt reinvestments, by itself, actually has a lot of accommodative power.	23	2
201510	2880	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Announcing your intention to explore the feasibility of negative interest rates—say, by as much as negative 50 basis points or negative 75 basis points—starts, by itself, to provide accommodation in states of the world in which I think investors are concerned that the FOMC will not be able to deliver.	23	2
201510	2881	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So I think there’s a lot of scope in terms of what one might do.	23	2
201510	2882	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The announcements I’m suggesting for this meeting, which would be a new round of asset purchases and an intention to explore the feasibility of negative interest rates, would come as a large surprise to market participants.	23	2
201510	2883	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We need to engender exactly such a surprise.	23	2
201510	2884	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It is clear from the data that market participants put significant weight on outcomes in which the FOMC will not take the actions that are necessary to achieve its objectives over long periods of time.	23	2
201510	2885	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It’s time for this Committee to prove market participants wrong on this point.	23	2
201510	2886	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Madam Chair, this is my last FOMC intervention.	23	2
201510	2887	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So if you’ll indulge me, I’d like to offer a final thought on communications for your consideration.	23	2
201510	2888	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Many of us around the table spend a considerable amount of time communicating with the public about our individual views on monetary policy.	23	2
201510	2889	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As someone who did a lot of this activity, I think this kind of communication is entirely appropriate.	23	2
201510	2890	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The public has a right to know the thinking of its representatives about these key policy questions.	23	2
201510	2891	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As well, for those of us who are presidents, this kind of communication helps provide a key link between the decisionmaking in this room and the far-flung residents of our various Districts.	23	2
201510	2892	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	However, this kind of communication does have its limitations.	23	2
201510	2893	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Most, if not all, of this communication offers the perspectives of individual participants about policy.	23	2
201510	2894	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	There is, I believe, a shortage of Committee communication that would provide the public with a sense of what the Committee has done and is likely to do in response to the evolution of economic conditions.	23	2
201510	2895	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The Chair is uniquely positioned to communicate to the public on behalf of the Committee.	23	2
201510	2896	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I believe that the public would have a better understanding of the likely evolution and direction of Committee decisions if it got to hear more from the Chair.	23	2
201510	2897	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I note that in 2005, according to FRASER, Chairman Greenspan gave 35 sets of remarks, testimonies, and speeches.	23	2
201510	2898	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The evolution of media technology and media focus suggests to me that the appropriate level of engagement is at least as high now and possibly much higher.	23	2
201510	2899	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think, too, that the evolution of the media means that this engagement needs to be more proactive than has been traditional.	23	2
201510	2900	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The communication needs develop, as we were just talking about in terms of miscommunications of the Committee’s intentions.	23	2
201510	2901	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The Committee has to fill that need, potentially on relatively short notice.	23	2
201510	2902	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Madam Chair, I have to say that you are uniquely positioned to communicate to the public on behalf of the Committee.	23	2

201510	2904	2015-10-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As my staff and I were able to experience during your recent visit to the Minneapolis Bank, you communicate with a rare clarity, a rare candor, and a rare genuine humanity and warmth.	23	2

201510	2914	2015-10-28	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Fischer.	23	2
201510	2915	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201510	2916	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	The outcome of this meeting should surprise no one.	23	2
201510	2917	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	We were not expected to start the normalization process at this meeting, and we should not and will not do that.	23	2
201510	2918	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	Rather, this is a scene-setting meeting at which we have first to review where we are and where we might be going and then to communicate our conclusions accurately to the public, the markets, and ourselves.	23	2
201510	2919	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	In September, we took a pause to evaluate recent developments in the global economy, particularly in China.	23	2
201510	2920	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	We can now conclude that the global economy is not at the start of a serious crisis; that global financial markets remained robust in the face of the September surprises; and that the external effect on US economic activity and inflation of foreign developments is likely to be substantial but not inconsistent with a continuation of economic growth, the strengthening of the labor markets, and a gradual return to our 2 percent inflation target.	23	2
201510	2921	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	By the time of the critical December decision, we will need to decide whether the employment reports for October and November that are due just over a week from now and early in December, respectively, are consistent with a continuation of economic growth and the strengthening of the labor market.	23	2
201510	2922	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	What numbers will we be looking for?	23	2
201510	2923	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	Well, staff calculations are that it would take hiring of roughly 50,000 to 75,000 a month to maintain the unemployment rate at 5.1 percent if the participation rate were to drift downward in parallel with its structural trend, and that it would take hiring of roughly 125,000 a month if the participation rate were to hold steady.	23	2
201510	2924	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	We might want to build in a cushion for these numbers, but they seem to me the right place to start, and I think we need some more clarity on this issue before the end of the meeting.	23	2
201510	2925	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	As usual, the staff has done an excellent job in producing the Tealbooks.	23	2
201510	2926	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	I believe the general feeling that things are not going well economically, as well as more generally, in the United States—which we sometimes hear around this table and elsewhere—is based in part on the expected slowing of economic growth.	23	2
201510	2927	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	One of the many interesting features of staff growth forecasts is the powerful effect of declines in participation on the aggregate growth rate.	23	2
201510	2928	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	That is clearly seen in the table “Decomposition of Potential GDP,” on page 26 of Tealbook A, in which the contribution from participation is forecast to decline 0.5 percentage point a year through 2018.	23	2
201510	2929	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	It’s also interesting that the contribution of the growth of multifactor productivity to overall growth is expected to rise only slowly from 0.3 percentage point this year to 0.7 percentage point in 2018, while the contribution of capital deepening to growth is expected to be constant at 0.8 percentage point—that is to say, more than double the rate of total factor productivity growth  from 2015 through 2017—and then to decline to 0.7 percentage point, the same as the contribution of TFP growth.	23	2
201510	2930	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	I take two messages from this.	23	2
201510	2931	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	First, economic growth is more in the hands of others than of the FOMC, something we all know but may, from time to time, forget.	23	2
201510	2932	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	Second, the effect of investment is potentially more powerful than I, at least, had thought.	23	2
201510	2933	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	These are messages we’re entitled to broadcast to a wider public.	23	2
201510	2934	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	On inflation, I have little to add to my previous comments, which were essentially that once the transitory effects of energy price and non-energy and food import price declines pass, we will be close to our target range.	23	2
201510	2935	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	Further, if the staff forecasts for the unemployment rate are correct—namely, a decline by 2017 to 4.7 percent unemployment—I believe we’re likely to move all of the way to 2 percent.	23	2
201510	2936	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	And we should also remind ourselves that not all shocks to inflation are negative.	23	2
201510	2937	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	They used to all be positive, and we will again see positive inflation shocks.	23	2
201510	2938	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	We just don’t know when.	23	2
201510	2939	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	I think we should also consider the risks to the forecast, but I’ll leave them aside for now and perhaps return to them during the general discussion of where we’re going.	23	2
201510	2940	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	I’d like to conclude with a few words on our communications coming out of this meeting.	23	2
201510	2941	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	I believe we should aim to influence expectations to the point at which the public and market participants expect us to move in December if our conditions are met, which could be translated into wanting expectations—and now I’m talking about probability—of an increase in the federal funds rate to rise to 50 percent or above after this meeting.	23	2
201510	2942	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	But—and now I’m talking not about communications to the public, but about what we need to do—we need also to begin preparing ourselves for the possibility that we will decide not to move in December.	23	2
201510	2943	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	And here, in the presence of President Kocherlakota, I think he must feel like Moses looking at the Promised Land with what I’m going to say.	23	2
201510	2944	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	[Laughter]	23	2
201510	2945	2015-10-28	meeting	TARULLO	He’s, regrettably, being exiled.	23	2
201510	2946	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	If we say nothing other than what we implied after the June and September meetings—that we will continue along the same path, waiting for the economy to strengthen—we may give the impression that we will not any time soon find conditions that would persuade us to move.	23	2
201510	2947	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	The message that three times—in June, September, and December—we’ve decided that the economy is too weak to raise the interest rate sends a disturbing message.	23	2
201510	2948	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	If we don’t move in December, we may need to say both to ourselves and to the public that we simply don’t like the path that the economy is on, and that we think we need to see stronger economic growth to be confident that inflation will return to our goal.	23	2
201510	2949	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	In short, we should consider moving to an expansionary monetary policy, one that will involve at least some of the measures that might be expansionary:  first, forward guidance regarding the path of the federal funds rate, provided that guidance is real or else carefully and expertly qualified; second, extending the maturity of our portfolio by lengthening the maturity of the Treasury obligations we hold, a move that Vice Chairman Dudley has mentioned several times; and, third, reducing the IOER rate and possibly the target range for the federal funds rate, though I doubt the wisdom of moving to a negative interest rate.	23	2
201510	2950	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	No doubt there are other measures to consider.	23	2
201510	2951	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	But part of the reason I’m concerned is that there is no other game in town than the Fed when it comes to policy relating to the macroeconomy at the moment.	23	2
201510	2952	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	We’re it—the only active policy player in town.	23	2
201510	2953	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	If we sit on the sidelines after we’ve reached the conclusion, for the third time, that the economy cannot withstand normalization, that message will be reinforced.	23	2
201510	2954	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	Rather, we should help get the economy to a situation from which it can normalize, for we are certainly not in a normal situation at present.	23	2
201510	2955	2015-10-28	meeting	FISCHER	Thank you.	23	2
201510	2956	2015-10-28	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2
201510	2957	2015-10-28	meeting	YELLEN	President Williams.	23	2
201510	2958	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201510	2959	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	I continue to prefer to take the first step in policy normalization at this time as described in alternative C.	23	2
201510	2960	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	At our September meeting, I argued that realized and expected progress toward our goals warranted liftoff.	23	2
201510	2961	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Incoming data reinforced that view.	23	2
201510	2962	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Labor markets continued to improve.	23	2
201510	2963	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Even at the slower pace of job growth we saw in the most recent report, we’ll overshoot full employment next year in my forecast.	23	2
201510	2964	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Other economic indicators, such as consumption and investment, are in line with my projections from our September meeting.	23	2
201510	2965	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Importantly, downside risks have also abated substantially as concerns about risks to the global economy have ebbed.	23	2
201510	2966	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Of course, inflation measures do remain low.	23	2
201510	2967	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	This is partly attributable to transitory factors, including dollar appreciation and drops in commodity prices, and those should dissipate over the course of this year and next year.	23	2
201510	2968	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	The waning of downward pressure from these factors, along with the continued improvement in the labor market, give me confidence inflation will move back to our 2 percent target over the medium term.	23	2
201510	2969	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	All in all, given the reduced downside risks from the global economy and my assessment that we’ll reach our inflation target and exceed our full employment mandate over the medium term, optimal policy dictates starting to raise rates soon.	23	2
201510	2970	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Indeed, most standard policy rules suggested raising rates some time ago.	23	2
201510	2971	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	While I find a case for liftoff at this meeting at least as compelling as December, I am willing to delay, again, what I would consider to be the appropriate policy action and go with alternative B as written.	23	2
201510	2972	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	One of my staff members had suggested to describe my mood as “grumpy.”	23	2
201510	2973	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	I was a little fearful that people would find one of the other dwarves to describe my mood or my behavior.	23	2
201510	2974	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	[Laughter]	23	2
201510	2975	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Picking up on some of the themes that Governor Fischer mentioned, we cannot continue this waiting strategy indefinitely.	23	2
201510	2976	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	We’re keeping financial markets on tenterhooks and, I think, sowing confusion.	23	2
201510	2977	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	I gave a lot of speeches and met with a lot of people, both our boards and members of the public, since our September meeting, and I was struck by how many times I heard, “You know, we thought you guys were raising rates, and we thought it made sense.	23	2
201510	2978	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now we really don’t understand.	23	2
201510	2979	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Do you know something about the economy that we don’t know?”	23	2
201510	2980	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	I said to my own board members, “Well, you know me.	23	2
201510	2981	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	We’re not that smart.”	23	2
201510	2982	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	But it is striking how difficult it is to convey—especially, I think, in our September statement, which I thought was actually a very good statement—this message that we are just sitting and waiting for something that people really don’t quite understand what we’re waiting for.	23	2
201510	2983	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, as our discussions make abundantly clear, the data and analysis will never be bulletproof.	23	2
201510	2984	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	There will always be uncertainties.	23	2
201510	2985	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	But, based on what I expect to see in the data in the next six weeks, I’m convinced it’ll be appropriate to lift off in December and—picking up on President Rosengren’s comment, which I agree with 100 percent—to signal when we go to C a “go slow” approach to further tightening over the next year as conditions unfold.	23	2
201510	2986	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	I am not only convinced that r* for the next couple of years is very low, but I also think there are significant odds that the longer-run r* is low.	23	2
201510	2987	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Those are arguments for being clearer about a very gradual or shallow path when we do raise rates.	23	2
201510	2988	2015-10-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you.	23	2

201510	2990	2015-10-28	meeting	YELLEN	President Rosengren.	23	2
201510	2991	2015-10-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201510	2992	2015-10-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	I support alternative B.	23	2
201510	2993	2015-10-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	The current language suggests to me, and may signal to financial markets, that unless the incoming data surprise to the downside, the Committee is prepared to raise rates at the December meeting.	23	2
201510	2994	2015-10-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	While this language nudges expectations toward raising rates in December, a nudge that I think is appropriate, it embodies the necessary flexibility to defer actions if incoming data indicate a more pronounced domestic slowdown than we currently expect.	23	2
201510	2995	2015-10-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	I do view the current language as signaling “probable” rather than “possible,” and that’s actually where I am in terms of my views.	23	2
201510	2996	2015-10-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	Like President Williams, I strongly prefer a gradual increase in removing accommodation.	23	2
201510	2997	2015-10-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	Waiting longer risks the need to remove accommodation more quickly, and, given the uncertainty discussed yesterday about the equilibrium real interest rate, a more rapid increase might run a greater risk of overshooting the equilibrium rate.	23	2
201510	2998	2015-10-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	In fact, I prefer a tightening cycle that is closer to the path currently predicted by the market, which would be a bit slower than the median SEP numbers in September.	23	2
201510	2999	2015-10-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	With inflation persistently lower than our 2 percent target, we have the luxury of removing accommodation more slowly than in previous tightening cycles.	23	2
201510	3000	2015-10-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	I would make the steepness of the interest rate path conditional on our confidence in reaching the inflation target.	23	2
201510	3001	2015-10-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	Even my currently expected gradual path is contingent on improved confidence in reaching the inflation target.	23	2
201510	3002	2015-10-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	Should our confidence in attaining that goal not improve in coming months or should we be surprised by a more rapid return toward An additional benefit from moving in December with a plan to move gradually is that we will have time to analyze the effectiveness of our monetary policy tightening tools.	23	2
201510	3003	2015-10-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	If we were to wait longer and need to potentially move rates at each meeting, we might have less flexibility to respond to surprises about the effectiveness of our tools or potential financial surprises from the initial tightening.	23	2
201510	3004	2015-10-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2

201510	3036	2015-10-28	meeting	LOCKHART	My guess is that the proposed paragraph 3 language without this reference will not send a strong enough signal to move market expectations from where they are today.	23	2

201510	3066	2015-10-28	meeting	TARULLO	I want to say a couple of things first, though, and they center on this issue of whether we now have to move because people have suggested we’re going to move and there was some expectation that we were going to move.	23	2
201510	3067	2015-10-28	meeting	TARULLO	I think the optimal approach to policymaking is, before you say something, to be pretty sure that what you say is what you’re going to do.	23	2
201510	3068	2015-10-28	meeting	TARULLO	But the second-best is not to go ahead and do something that is ill advised because you suggested to people beforehand that you might do it.	23	2
201510	3069	2015-10-28	meeting	TARULLO	The second best is to treat your earlier suggestion as essentially some variation on a sunk cost and then go ahead and do what makes sense.	23	2
201510	3070	2015-10-28	meeting	TARULLO	The first point I’d make is that this, to some degree, is a self-inflicted wound.	23	2
201510	3071	2015-10-28	meeting	TARULLO	I agree with people who have said that there’s a lot of confusion out there, and that there was an expectation as well as a lot of discussion centering on September.	23	2
201510	3072	2015-10-28	meeting	TARULLO	How could the markets and the commentators not be focused on September when so many of us were out talking about September?	23	2
201510	3073	2015-10-28	meeting	TARULLO	This notion that, “Gee, the markets have focused on September—we’d better do it,” is somehow linked to the way in which our public statements have been date and calendar centered rather than talking about the narratives, as I put it yesterday, or the outlook, as many of you refer to it, that would guide our sense of when it’s appropriate to move.	23	2
201510	3074	2015-10-28	meeting	TARULLO	There is a lot to what President Williams and others have said about there being some sense of, do we know something that the markets don’t know?	23	2

201510	3147	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	Implicit in that is that if the economy continues on the current path, with job growth sufficient to continue to materially reduce labor market slack, I would support liftoff at the December meeting, and I would present such a decision in a context of a very broad agreement among the membership of the Committee that the path of rate increases will be a gradual one.	23	2
201510	3148	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	For me, the tightening cycle can be very slow.	23	2
201510	3149	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	The market path does not trouble me, although, of course, the data will dictate that.	23	2
201510	3150	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	The question is, why move at all in December?	23	2
201510	3151	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	Why not wait another three months or six months—or even a year or two years?	23	2
201510	3152	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	And I would offer two considerations.	23	2
201510	3153	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	First, I believe that the test that we’ve articulated will be met if we get one more cycle of solid data.	23	2
201510	3154	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	I also believe that a well-telegraphed move of 25 basis points, presented in a context of a very broad Committee consensus favoring a shallow path, should not have a sustained material effect on financial conditions.	23	2
201510	3155	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	Second, I would point to the Committee’s own communication, and let me be clear: I’m not arguing here that we should mistakenly do this because we’ve said we would.	23	2
201510	3156	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	I’m arguing that, in a close call, I would lean toward going if we get a chance to do that.	23	2
201510	3157	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	I don’t think it would be a mistake.	23	2
201510	3158	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	The reason is, we’ve carefully guided the public to expect liftoff this year.	23	2
201510	3159	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	Many on the Committee, including me and many others, have publicly embraced that expectation.	23	2
201510	3160	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	The September SEP has 13 of the 17 of us supporting liftoff this year.	23	2
201510	3161	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	In the September SEP, we had median expectations regarding second-half real GDP growth of 2 percent and unemployment at 5 percent.	23	2
201510	3162	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	Those will be met, hypothetically.	23	2
201510	3163	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	I think there will be a cost to appearing to change our minds, and we would simply need to weigh the benefits against that cost.	23	2
201510	3164	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	I guess I would really like to move past this essentially tactical decision about the precise date of liftoff and shift the focus toward the very broad agreement about the gradual path.	23	2
201510	3165	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	With that backdrop—and here I echo what others have said—I suspect that a decision not to move in December will not be, and will not be seen by the public as, just another step in a data-driven, meeting-by-meeting evaluation of policy but rather a fundamental change in the Committee’s framework as it’s been expressed in communications this year.	23	2
201510	3166	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	One implication would be a sense that we are seriously troubled by the path of the economy.	23	2
201510	3167	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	An additional implication would be a significant further period at the effective lower bound.	23	2
201510	3168	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	Any restatement of our objective function risks setting the bar at a level that may not be met for a year or more.	23	2
201510	3169	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	In addition to the costs of appearing to change our mind, I am concerned with the buildup of financial and economic imbalances over time if, in fact, we’re going to remain at the zero lower bound for an extended period.	23	2
201510	3170	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	The question is how high to set the bar for incoming data between now and the December meeting—particularly on two payroll reports, if I can admit that.	23	2
201510	3171	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	I would simply say that I would not be setting it excessively high.	23	2
201510	3172	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	I’ll end with the thought that I really do believe it’s essential that for the period ahead we see economic growth above its trend rate.	23	2
201510	3173	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	Otherwise, I’m not sure why we are raising the federal funds rate.	23	2
201510	3174	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	But if we do see that by some reasonable margin, I will be prepared to go forward.	23	2
201510	3175	2015-10-28	meeting	POWELL	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201510	3176	2015-10-28	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2
201510	3177	2015-10-28	meeting	YELLEN	President Mester.	23	2
201510	3178	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201510	3179	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	There’s been little change in my medium-run outlook, and I continue to believe there’s a good case for moving policy off the zero lower bound.	23	2
201510	3180	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	In my view, the criteria we’ve set out for liftoff have been met.	23	2
201510	3181	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	Such a move is consistent with the Tealbook’s optimal control simulations, which balance the macroeconomic risks of lifting off too early versus too late, and with various versions of monetary policy rules.	23	2
201510	3182	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	We have already taken out insurance against downside risks by keeping interest rates considerably lower than prescriptions from almost all of the policy rules, even as the Tealbook-consistent estimate of r* has been rising.	23	2
201510	3183	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	This estimate moved up more than 25 basis points to 74 basis points in this Tealbook.	23	2
201510	3184	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	The funds rate remains well below estimates of the longer-run equilibrium rate.	23	2
201510	3185	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	In addition, even if they are not imminent, there are likely to be some building risks to financial stability from keeping rates low for a long time.	23	2
201510	3186	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	We need to be cognizant of these even if they are not in our models and are difficult to measure.	23	2
201510	3187	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	Indeed, we have said in our own Monetary Policy Reports that we consider this a potential cost of the necessary extraordinary monetary policy actions we took during the crisis and recession.	23	2
201510	3188	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	Yesterday’s discussion of r* suggests that there are good reasons to think that the natural rate of interest may be lower than it’s been historically and perhaps significantly lower.	23	2
201510	3189	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	Given the shocks that inevitably hit the economy, this means the odds of getting pushed to the effective lower bound are higher than they’ve been historically.	23	2
201510	3190	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	To deal with the recent crisis and recession, the Federal Reserve developed a set of monetary policy tools that can be used in such situations.	23	2
201510	3191	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	There are many studies showing that these tools were effective in easing monetary and financial conditions, and I’d like us to be in a position to be able to use these tools again if we ever find ourselves in a situation in which they’re needed.	23	2
201510	3192	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	However, there continues to be some skepticism about the efficacy of these tools.	23	2
201510	3193	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	Ultimately, the verdict will depend on demonstrating that there is a way out.	23	2
201510	3194	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	Failure to navigate a good exit has the potential to take these tools off the table.	23	2
201510	3195	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	This risk is another factor that persuades me to favor taking an initial action to raise rates rather than waiting too long or too much longer, even in the face of some uncertainty regarding the outlook.	23	2
201510	3196	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	I’d rather address those uncertainties by adjusting the slope of the policy rate path after liftoff, if need be, because of shocks as we learn more about the longer- run growth of the economy and r*.	23	2
201510	3197	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	Liftoff remains an unlikely outcome at today’s meeting.	23	2
201510	3198	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	Our next decision point is December.	23	2
201510	3199	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	The public is going to be looking at today’s statement as providing information about what we need to see between now and December in order to lift off.	23	2
201510	3200	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	Have we gotten closer to meeting the criteria for liftoff or not?	23	2
201510	3201	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	If I saw data similar to what we saw in this intermeeting period—including payrolls in the 140,000 range or even lower, above the 125,000 that the Tealbook staff has said is necessary to keep the unemployment rate constant—I’d be prepared to raise the federal funds rate in December.	23	2
201510	3202	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	However, others may see things differently, and the statement needs to convey a sense of the consensus view.	23	2
201510	3203	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	I admit the communications in this environment are very challenging, but we should always be taking steps to meet those challenges.	23	2
201510	3204	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	I believe that the public read a more negative outlook in our September FOMC statement than was intended.	23	2
201510	3205	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	The guessing game coming into that meeting reminded me of the old Clairol hair color tag line: “Does she or doesn’t she?”	23	2
201510	3206	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	That tag line actually won an advertising award.	23	2
201510	3207	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	I’m not sure we can say the same about our own communications.	23	2
201510	3208	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	[Laughter]	23	2
201510	3209	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	My main concern with the language in alternative B is that the characterization of labor market developments will convey a more negative message than we intend and set up the wrong expectations.	23	2
201510	3210	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	The first paragraph drops language stating whether we’ve seen labor market improvement since September and then cites the slowdown in payroll growth and no change in the unemployment rate.	23	2
201510	3211	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	Payrolls continue to grow above trend.	23	2
201510	3212	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	Payroll growth of 140,000 per month, if sustained, should put downward pressure on the unemployment rate, and, in this stage of the business cycle, slowing in the pace of job gains is to be expected.	23	2
201510	3213	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	It’s a feature of many economic forecasts, including the Tealbook and the Federal Reserve Bank of Cleveland staff model.	23	2
201510	3214	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	Indeed, I interpreted the adjustment we made in the liftoff criteria in July, changing “further improvement” to “some further improvement,” as a recognition that we expected the pace of gains to slow.	23	2
201510	3215	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	In addition, other measures of unemployment continued to decline since our September meeting.	23	2
201510	3216	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	By omitting these relevant facts, the tone is negative, and the public may infer we have moved further from meeting the labor market condition for liftoff.	23	2
201510	3217	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	I fear we’re feeding expectations that monthly job gains close to 200,000 are needed for us to conclude there’s been some further improvement in the labor market.	23	2
201510	3218	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	If that’s true, we should say so.	23	2
201510	3219	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	Essentially, what we’ve done is to add another liftoff criterion by suggesting that the second derivative of employment, and not just the first derivative, matters.	23	2
201510	3220	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	If it’s not true, then it’s a problem allowing that expectation to stand.	23	2
201510	3221	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	So let me offer a suggestion—I know I’m tilting at windmills—that we change the characterization of labor markets by saying: “While the pace of job gains slowed last month, the pace is consistent with some further improvement in the labor market.	23	2
201510	3222	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	The unemployment rate held steady, while other measures of underemployment declined.”	23	2
201510	3223	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	I think this characterization is consistent with the facts and conveys the proper sentiment.	23	2
201510	3224	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	Regarding the other changes suggested in alternative B, I support making the change in paragraph 3, and I favor saying “later this year” instead of “at its next meeting.”	23	2
201510	3225	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	Out of an abundance of caution, we do take market expectations into account in our decisions to lift off.	23	2
201510	3226	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	I understand that.	23	2
201510	3227	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	So I think we do need to change expectations in order to keep December alive.	23	2
201510	3228	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	I believe that the language does offer us flexibility if the data disappoint and our outlook changes.	23	2

201510	3230	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	In paragraph 1, I have a small preference for saying “slightly” to characterize the change in market-based measures of inflation compensation to acknowledge that the decline was smaller over this intermeeting period than it was last time—10 basis points versus 20 basis points.	23	2
201510	3231	2015-10-28	meeting	MESTER	Finally, if the Committee truly believes it’s unlikely that we will have enough information by December to make a judgment about progress toward our goals and therefore to make a liftoff decision, then let’s say so now rather than setting up another round of the guessing game.	23	2

201510	3314	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	To fix ideas, I said, “Well, I suppose if you look at the dot chart, you might think that, at the end of 2016, a funds rate of about 1½ might not be unreasonable,” and they almost gasped.	23	2
201510	3315	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	It was such a large number, basically, was what they were saying.	23	2
201510	3316	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	Again, others have said this, too.	23	2
201510	3317	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	There’s a desire to get off of zero, but how high is really up in the air, and it’s not nearly as high as some people probably think.	23	2
201510	3318	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	I’m sorry—did I mention that I have “over 11:15” in the pool for when this ends?	23	2
201510	3319	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	[Laughter]	23	2
201510	3320	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	I’ll try to cut some things out, I promise.	23	2
201510	3321	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	Now, let me say again why communicating a shallow policy rate path is appropriate.	23	2
201510	3322	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	First, the r* memos and our discussion yesterday made a strong risk-management case for keeping rates low in order to help avoid bad outcomes associated with the effective lower bound on interest rates.	23	2
201510	3323	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	For me, this is a powerful argument, because it captures the asymmetry in the risks we face.	23	2
201510	3324	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	That is, currently, I’m not hearing many discussions of similarly bad outcomes on the other side of the ledger.	23	2
201510	3325	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	If you are worried about high inflation, even if events changed quickly and underlying inflation was headed to 3 percent or even 4 percent, our interest rate policy tools could be employed effectively to rein it in.	23	2
201510	3326	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	There’s a second reason why I support an aggressive commitment to a symmetric 2 percent inflation objective.	23	2
201510	3327	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	It’s that we are likely in a regime in which even during normal times we could all too often run out of capacity to lower the funds rate to deal with recessionary shocks or below-target inflation.	23	2
201510	3328	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	Longer-run measures of r* are plausibly in the range of 1 to 1½ percent.	23	2
201510	3329	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	So, with our inflation objective of 2 percent over the longer run, the nominal federal funds rate ought to average about 3 to 3½ percent.	23	2
201510	3330	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	This means our monetary policy capacity on the accommodative side is only 350 basis points.	23	2
201510	3331	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	This is a brave, new, risky world for FOMC recession fighting.	23	2
201510	3332	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	In the period that included the 1990–91 recession, the Greenspan FOMC lowered the funds rate from a peak of 9¾ percent to 3 percent.	23	2
201510	3333	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	That’s 675 basis points.	23	2
201510	3334	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	They were a little bit above steady state.	23	2
201510	3335	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	In the cycle that included the 2000 recession, the Greenspan FOMC lowered the funds rate from a peak of 6½ percent to 1 percent.	23	2
201510	3336	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	That’s 550 basis points.	23	2
201510	3337	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	In the most recent cycle, the Bernanke FOMC lowered the funds rate more than 500 basis points, and we clearly wanted to do much more.	23	2
201510	3338	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	We instead resorted to increasing our balance sheet to about $4½ trillion.	23	2
201510	3339	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	The point is that having only 300 to 350 basis points of room to lower the funds rate to zero from a neutral level will likely pose a serious challenge for our future recession-fighting and inflation-inducing capabilities.	23	2
201510	3340	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	Historically, 350 basis points has not been enough.	23	2
201510	3341	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	I agree with the suggestions given by Presidents Williams and Rosengren yesterday that we need to review our tools for more regular use at the effective lower bound.	23	2
201510	3342	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	Well, I’ve got more comments on symmetry, but I’ll skip those.	23	2
201510	3343	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	These issues inform my strong conviction that we need to make sure our policy rate path over the next 12 to 18 months is appropriately accommodative.	23	2
201510	3344	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	We need the time to assess domestic and global risks that we might normally discount, but that today impose asymmetric losses due to the constraints of the effective lower bound.	23	2
201510	3345	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	And we need the time that a shallow path allows to make sure inflation is heading to our target in a symmetric fashion and not stalling out in a way that would even further impinge on our ability to fight future recessions or disinflations.	23	2
201510	3346	2015-10-28	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2

201510	3366	2015-10-28	meeting	BULLARD	Today the national unemployment rate is 5.1 percent, very close to historical norms and well below the median unemployment rate over the past 50 years in the United States, which is 5.8 percent.	23	2

201510	3369	2015-10-28	meeting	BULLARD	So, again, net of the oil shock, inflation is actually pretty close to target.	23	2
201510	3370	2015-10-28	meeting	BULLARD	Arguably, this is about as good as the Committee has ever done with respect to its goals, yet the Committee has not moved to try to normalize either the balance sheet or the policy rate, even though both dimensions of our goals are arguably relatively close to normal.	23	2
201510	3371	2015-10-28	meeting	BULLARD	The private sector may reasonably conclude, or may be forgiven for concluding, that we intend to keep the zero interest rate policy, or ZIRP, at least through the medium term.	23	2
201510	3372	2015-10-28	meeting	BULLARD	Even with liftoff, as Governor Powell and others emphasized yesterday, the pace of rate increases is likely to be so gradual that a moderately negative shock would easily compel the Committee to return to the zero lower bound.	23	2
201510	3373	2015-10-28	meeting	BULLARD	My point is that the probabilities are fairly high at this juncture that we will simply keep ZIRP—or, if not ZIRP, near-ZIRP—in place.	23	2

201510	3375	2015-10-28	meeting	BULLARD	All of us—the Committee and the staff—have in our heads that we’re going to return to the equilibrium of the 1980s and 1990s, which we know and love, and that we’re going to move the funds rate around according to typical policy prescriptions from that era.	23	2

201510	3453	2015-10-28	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Brainard.	23	2
201510	3454	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201510	3455	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	I see the state of the economy as well as the outlook as very similar to what we faced in September.	23	2
201510	3456	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	Improvements in resource utilization look to be gradual, and the recent data on inflation continue to suggest an underlying trend below our 2 percent target.	23	2
201510	3457	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	Important downside risks to the outlook for activity and inflation remain, with global economic growth decelerating and key foreign economies continuing to face difficult challenges.	23	2
201510	3458	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	It’s not yet clear what effect on US activity the recent slowing in global growth will have.	23	2
201510	3459	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	As a result and with the deterioration in inflation compensation, I’m not yet reasonably confident that inflation will return to 2 percent over the medium term, and I think it’s appropriate to keep the federal funds rate in its current target range while we receive more information on the resilience of the underlying momentum in the economy.	23	2
201510	3460	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	For some time, there’s been a conversation concerning the normalization of monetary policy that equates normalization with moving off the zero lower bound and tightening.	23	2
201510	3461	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	I think the discussion of the natural rate of interest yesterday grounds that discussion in terms of the distance of the effective federal funds rate relative to a time-varying natural rate of interest.	23	2
201510	3462	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	We’ve discussed a host of reasons why that natural rate of interest might be low at the moment and might remain somewhat low in the medium term, ranging from the empirical estimates that have been circulated to the Committee, to the persistent financial headwinds of the crisis, to the observation that world interest rates appear to have moved quite low and exerted a downward pull on US interest rates by the exchange rate and financial market channels.	23	2
201510	3463	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	On balance, the materials developed for the Committee’s consideration suggest important reasons why our current monetary policy stance may be closer to neutral than may be implied by conventional monetary policy empirical regularities based on historical relationships.	23	2
201510	3464	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	Importantly, the asymmetry in risk-management considerations also argues for being somewhat cautious.	23	2
201510	3465	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	The persistence of the forces holding down r* suggests it will remain low relative to historical norms.	23	2
201510	3466	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	This, together with downside risks from abroad, points toward an elevated risk of being constrained in the future by a lower bound on policy rates.	23	2
201510	3467	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	In those circumstances, prudence dictates ensuring that momentum in real activity and inflation is robust enough to withstand adverse shocks before initiating a tightening cycle.	23	2
201510	3468	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	If risks were skewed in the opposite direction—if there were a sufficiently large chance that policy would have to tighten unusually rapidly in response to an abrupt tightening in resource utilization and a substantial buildup in inflationary pressures—then it would be prudent to begin lifting off to guard against the risks to the stability of the economy.	23	2
201510	3469	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	However, given that inflation has run persistently below our target, that inflation breakevens have moved down substantially and persistently, that wage and other indicators suggest that slack is diminishing but still remains, that estimates of the effect of resource utilization on inflation are relatively modest at present, and that r* is estimated to be lower than historical norms, I believe that risk to be somewhat modest.	23	2
201510	3470	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	Even rapid tightening in today’s circumstances would be well within the norm of historical tightening cycles.	23	2
201510	3471	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	A possible reason for lifting off is a desire to move away from the zero lower bound, perhaps because there is a stigma or a discomfort associated with that policy setting.	23	2
201510	3472	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	I think those who are influenced by this view but are also concerned about risk management, given a low medium-term r* and substantial downside risks to demand, might recommend lifting off and then moving very slowly.	23	2
201510	3473	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	That has some merits, but it also carries substantial risks of resulting in excessive tightening in financial conditions, especially given the possibility of an excessive reaction through foreign exchange values.	23	2
201510	3474	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	My own perspective on this, I’d have to say, is colored by the many episodes in other advanced economies of raising, reversal, and regret.	23	2
201510	3475	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	These considerations lead me to want to be somewhat more confident before we initiate a tightening path, which argues for waiting another meeting or two to gauge the underlying momentum of domestic demand.	23	2
201510	3476	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	Since March, we’ve stated that the timing of liftoff is data dependent, and I believe it is advisable to maintain this stance.	23	2
201510	3477	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	It’s possible that the data we receive between now and the December meeting will justify lifting off or keeping the policy rate at its current level.	23	2
201510	3478	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	With regard to the communications and recognizing there is considerable sentiment in this room in favor of a December liftoff and legitimate concern to ensure that markets are on notice, I agree with the desire to make sure that a liftoff in December is viewed as possible, although not too probable.	23	2
201510	3479	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	So maybe I’m in the 55 percent range.	23	2
201510	3480	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	As against this, I believe it is inadvisable to reintroduce calendar-based guidance after working so carefully and deliberately to eliminate it.	23	2
201510	3481	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	For those reasons, I’m a bit concerned about introducing language regarding “later this year” or “at its next meeting,” which we will then potentially have to remove if it gets stale very quickly and which in turn risks reinforcing perceptions of “lurchiness” in our communications.	23	2
201510	3482	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	I actually think the new version of the sentence in paragraph 3 without either version of the bracketed language will clearly put market participants on notice that the Committee is actively debating a rate rise at the next meeting.	23	2
201510	3483	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	The suggestions by President Lockhart and by President Rosengren did a nice job of balancing these two considerations, and I would probably put those suggestions above either of the versions currently on the table.	23	2
201510	3484	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	With regard to my preference for the wording of those bracketed items on the table, I would probably put “at its next meeting” slightly above “later this year,” because of the possibility that we could carry it forward.	23	2
201510	3485	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	The final thing I would say is, I think the perceptions of “lurchiness” in our communications had as much to do with intermeeting communications by participants as they did with the way that we reacted to incoming data.	23	2
201510	3486	2015-10-28	meeting	BRAINARD	I, for one, would have been very reluctant to utter any calendar-based statement in the days and months leading up to this meeting, and I would be very happy to continue taking a pledge not to utter any calendar-based statements myself if other members of the Committee also wanted to leave to the Chair the sole voice on any calendar-based prognostications between now and December.	23	2

201510	3493	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	The statement makes it clear that we’re still data dependent.	23	2
201510	3494	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	It gives us a chance to parse that data and decide whether we think the economy has sufficient forward momentum to justify liftoff or not.	23	2
201510	3495	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	If the data are consistent with lifting off, then I would anticipate that expectations about December would shift up as we approach the meeting.	23	2
201510	3496	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	But if this doesn’t happen sufficiently on its own, then I think we should give the markets a nudge.	23	2
201510	3497	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	My own view is that, in December, we want market participants to be expecting liftoff if we are planning to lift off or not expecting liftoff if we’re not planning to lift off.	23	2
201510	3498	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	This is how we behaved historically, and, given our recent track record on communications, this is very important if we’re going to enhance our credibility with the public.	23	2
201510	3499	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	In terms of language, I favor “slightly” in paragraph 1 because, as someone said—I guess it was Loretta—10 basis points is less than 20 basis points.	23	2
201510	3500	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	In terms of “later this year” and “at its next meeting,” that’s a really tricky one.	23	2
201510	3501	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I like “at its next meeting” better because I think it’s more explicit, but, on the other hand, I take Governor Tarullo’s point that it’s a lot easier to take out “later this year” than it is to take out “at its next meeting,” because it has to come out automatically.	23	2
201510	3502	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	So I guess if push came to shove, I’d be in favor of “later this year” because of the ease of taking it out of the statement.	23	2
201510	3503	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	You don’t have to live with “at its next meeting.”	23	2
201510	3504	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	If we take out “at its next meeting” and we don’t move in December, then people are going to find that quite noteworthy.	23	2
201510	3505	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I do like the “based on incoming data.”	23	2
201510	3506	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	We’ve said we’re data dependent.	23	2
201510	3507	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	It’s a little weird now to all of a sudden say, “Well, the data are really noisy, so we’re not going to pay attention to them.”	23	2
201510	3508	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	It’s not saying we’re going to just take the data literally.	23	2
201510	3509	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	It’s saying we’re going to use the data to assess our progress, both realized and expected.	23	2
201510	3510	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	So it’s only to the extent that the data inform our views of the progress, both realized and expected, that we’re going to consider those data.	23	2
201510	3511	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	Talking about the data is important because we want market participants to react to the incoming data to assess the probability of liftoff.	23	2
201510	3512	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	We want them to think right along with us.	23	2
201510	3513	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, we know what we’ll do if the economy continues to grow at an above-trend pace and the labor market tightens further.	23	2
201510	3514	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	As I said yesterday, I think we also have to come up with some good answers of how we’ll respond, if the economy doesn’t cooperate, to the potential assertion that we’re going to be out of weapons.	23	2
201510	3515	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	We need to have a “plan B” just in case, and we need to have more discussion among the Committee participants about what that plan B might consist of, because if we don’t move in December, the next question for the Chair is going to be, “Okay, so what are you going to do if the economy continues to disappoint?”	23	2
201510	3516	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	The more full and credible answer she can give, the more reassuring it will be to confidence.	23	2
201510	3517	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	There are a number of options worth considering.	23	2
201510	3518	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I’m just going to run through a bunch of options to put them on the table.	23	2
201510	3519	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	The first is the very obvious one:  We could extend the duration of our balance sheet.	23	2
201510	3520	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	The Treasury securities have been aging.	23	2
201510	3521	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	We have a lot of Treasury securities maturing next year.	23	2
201510	3522	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	So, clearly, extending the duration is a real, live possibility.	23	2
201510	3523	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	When we consider extending duration, a lot of times we think, “Well, we’ll let the short-dated Treasury securities mature and then invest in longer-term Treasury securities, or we’ll sell the short-dated Treasury securities and invest in longer-term Treasury securities.”	23	2
201510	3524	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	But there’s also another MEP program:  We could sell short-dated Treasury securities and buy agency mortgage-backed securities.	23	2
201510	3525	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	That’s another possibility that I think we should at least look into, because it may turn out to have a more powerful effect on economic activity than just buying Treasury securities.	23	2
201510	3526	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I said “look into,”	23	2
201510	3527	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	President Lacker, not necessarily “do.”	23	2
201510	3528	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	[Laughter]	23	2
201510	3529	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	You’ll have your day in court if we go down this path.	23	2
201510	3530	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	If we were to decide to extend the duration of the portfolio, it’s also going to be very important in terms of how we message this.	23	2
201510	3531	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	We don’t want people to conclude that we’re extending our duration because we somehow have this balance sheet constraint.	23	2
201510	3532	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	If you’re going to talk about extending duration, you also have to say that’s the first step in what would be subsequent potential steps to actually expand the balance sheet and do large-scale asset purchases.	23	2
201510	3533	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	If we don’t talk about that at all, people will reach the conclusion that the reason you’re extending the duration is that somehow you have this very solid balance sheet limitation.	23	2
201510	3534	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I think that would not be reassuring to people.	23	2
201510	3535	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	That would actually be somewhat alarming to people.	23	2
201510	3536	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	In terms of another large LSAP program, I’ve never heard anything compelling about why the current balance sheet size is the limit.	23	2
201510	3537	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	If someone has a really strong argument for why this is the limit, I’d like to hear it.	23	2
201510	3538	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	But it seems to me that $4½ trillion or $5½ trillion—it’s not obvious that we’re out of ammunition here.	23	2
201510	3539	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	And, to me, if the option was to be stuck at the zero lower bound indefinitely with inflation far below our objective versus more QE that could maybe avert that outcome, I would favor more QE, thank you.	23	2
201510	3540	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	The IOER rate is more controversial.	23	2
201510	3541	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	We could cut the IOER rate.	23	2
201510	3542	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	We could probably cut it into negative territory.	23	2
201510	3543	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	We decided not to do this earlier because of concerns about the unintended consequences, but maybe the European experience makes us more comfortable that the costs are less than we’d feared.	23	2
201510	3544	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	So I would encourage the staff to work on updating our view of the costs and benefits of a reduction in the IOER rate.	23	2
201510	3545	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	We could even say in our communications, if the economy were to disappoint, “We’re looking at this.	23	2
201510	3546	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	This is potentially on the table, and we’ll be back to you on that.”	23	2
201510	3547	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	The last thing I would point to—and this is going to be a little bit more controversial—is that I think we should consider price-level targeting.	23	2
201510	3548	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I really do.	23	2
201510	3549	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	If things get bad and you’re worried about inflation expectations getting unanchored to the downside, price-level targeting is a strategy to lean against that and is particularly relevant in the current environment because we’ve been underperforming on our inflation goals for quite some time.	23	2
201510	3550	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	The current policy of bygones—that we just forgive all of the past misses on inflation—does run the risk over time of having inflation expectations become unanchored to the downside.	23	2
201510	3551	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	A PLT policy pushes against that.	23	2
201510	3552	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I think we discussed that a few years ago.	23	2
201510	3553	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	We decided not to go there because we thought it was hard to explain, but my own personal view is that it’s not that hard to explain.	23	2
201510	3554	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	If you’re really worried about inflation expectations getting unanchored to the downside, it is actually a pretty credible tool to address this.	23	2
201510	3555	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	Finally, in extremis, if all of these tools were insufficient, we probably should call a spade a spade and say to the Congress and the Administration, “Look, monetary policy can only do so much.	23	2

201510	3557	2015-10-28	meeting	DUDLEY	For example, a pretty strong argument can be made for a large infrastructure investment program if you have a very low level of interest rates.	23	2

201510	3869	2015-10-28	meeting	YELLEN	Before we take a vote, if you would permit me a couple of words to wrap up the policy round, I would like to say a few words about communications.	23	2

201510	3873	2015-10-28	meeting	YELLEN	And I believe it’s exceptionally important to maintain discipline in our communications.	23	2
201510	3874	2015-10-28	meeting	YELLEN	Following up on what President Kocherlakota said earlier, I think our objective should be to try to make clear where we stand as a Committee.	23	2
201510	3875	2015-10-28	meeting	YELLEN	That principle is the very first guideline contained in our policy on external communications— namely, every Committee participant has an obligation to enhance the public’s understanding of monetary policy, including its rationale.	23	2
201510	3876	2015-10-28	meeting	YELLEN	I think today’s statement means that, although no decision has been made on December, it very well may be appropriate to move at our next meeting if nothing new and unexpected happens to alter the outlook and the incoming data support our expectation that the economy is growing above trend and will continue to do so, with the labor market continuing to improve at an acceptable pace.	23	2
201510	3877	2015-10-28	meeting	YELLEN	Our statement indicates to the markets that December is a “live” possibility, but also, importantly, that no decision has been made.	23	2
